<rating>1< /rating>< Review>
Our dog had been throwing up and was diagnosed by Banfield as having a "sensitive stomach."  They prescribed special food (which they also sell).  Over several months, Quincy didn't get any better.  He was going downhill and I felt he was gravely ill.  I wanted to take him to another vet, but my wife had a health care contract with them.  They said he needed a lot of testing, a radiograph, and a consultant to interpet it.  They said we should upgrade his health care to include some of the tests.  We did.  We came back several hours later.  They said they were concerned about some of the tests.  We saw the X-ray which showed a lot of air in his stomach.  But they didn't know what was wrong.  It would have to wait for the consultant (extra cost not covered by the upgraded health policy).  They sent him to VCA Animal Hospital to be observed overnight because of the air.  On arriving at VCA, the vet took one look at Quincy and knew he was gravely ill.  It took all of five minutes using ultrasound to diagnose a massive tumor filling the abdominal cavity.  The vet said when the muscles and rest of the dog is wasted away, but one area is growing that is a red flag.  He said Quincy was at "the end," and needed to be put down immediately.  There was no choice, we didn't want him to suffer.  I do not understand how Banfield could miss all this.  Perhaps they should spend less time selling insurance, consultant fees, and pet food, and pay more attention to the animal itself.</Review>

<resp>None<//resp>< review>
Thanks to a friend telling me about a Bristol Farms Grocery Store opening soon in Yorba Linda, and subsequently seeing Yelper, Nick H.'s review during soft opening, I learned about the Grand Opening of Bristol Farms today in Yorba Linda, CA.

I've been a Bristol Farms customer for over 30 years.  I was excited to hear about the Grand Opening for their newest store.

I arrived 10 minutes to 9 AM and waited with hundreds and hundreds of people in line for the doors to open at 9 AM as promised. We stood for over 40 minutes, it was not until after 9:30 that the line started moving.

The allure of a free canvas bag for the first 300 customers sounded great, but they gave tickets out to those folks who arrived bright and early BUT they failed to let the other hundreds and hundreds of people who were patiently waiting in line know NOT to wait in line but just proceed to enter and start shopping in the store.  Bristol, for future grand openings, please keep this in mind.  A lot of us felt our time was wasted and or just left and went home.

I stayed, helped a 90 year old elderly lady into the store to avoid heat stroke from standing in line outside in the sun too long, and somehow managed to enjoy the store despite the overcrowding of customers.  I grabbed a bagel, cream cheese, and coffee and had a seat at their indoor dining area.

Samples, as always with Bristol Farms, were generous.  Since I was in between breakfast and lunch I visited other stores in the shopping center and waited for my husband to join me for lunch at Bristol.

We ordered a Banh Mi Sandwich made with 10 hour roasted Pork.  The flavors were not as stand out as I would have hoped for, I was disappointed in the flavors of the sandwich.  Not enough punch in the pickled veggies of the sandwich.

Although the store was staffed more than adequately, there was trouble ringing up coupons, etc. as some cashiers were still learning the system.

The best things about Bristol are: Produce, Meats, Cheese and THE COOKIE (like a double tree cookie on steroids).  Apparently for the next three weeks the're running some great store deals.  Also email sign ups provide coupons for free items, like the dozen eggs I got for free today.

For grocery stores, it is hard to beat Bristol Farms in quality of produce and food items, I just wished my sandwich tasted better!</review>

<date>1587720689976< /date>< Review>
Food: I order the Caprese Panini with Chicken and a side of Black beans. Juicey chicken breast, melted mozzarella cheese, tomato, basil, dressed in signature pesto sauce and between 2 toasted slices of bread. My favorite lunch item and the beans are a nice little touch to round the meal off. For dessert, I get the French Toast and it is s favorite among my friends. Lastly,  I get a Bloody Mary to help start my day.

Service and Atmosphere: The place is cute and pretty small but there is also outside seating. If there is a wait, stick around because the attentive and fast service will get you seated in no time.

Final Thought: I dig the place but some of the items can get a little pricey and the portions don't justify the cost. But it is a yummy and trendy place, so it is, what it is.< /Review>

<Text>Food: I order the Caprese Panini with Chicken and a side of Black beans. <name>Chloe E</name><time>1542497427613</time><rating>3</rating>< Review>
My boyfriend and I showed up on a Saturday morning-ish, around 11:30. We were told that it was a 30 minute wait. After some time (didn‚Äôt keep track but we were very hungry) we were offered to sit at the bar, we declined and were set on table seating. The restaurant itself is cute, nicely decorated and has a Wes Anderson movie playing on a tv behind the bar.
After getting seated and being served a glass of water (we had gotten coffee while waiting for our table) we were then informed that they were out of the breakfast potatoes and the eggs Benedict (and a couple other items) this was around 12-12:30.
The entire reason for visiting this particular place is because the eggs Benedict were so highly praised, so to say the least we were disappointed.
Instead I ordered the Wilshire omelette with hash browns (other option would have been breakfast potatoes) my boyfriend ordered the quiche of the day which happened to be the Wilshire quiche.
Our orders arrived quickly but the eggs in my omelette were significantly over cooked and the quiche was very spinach heavy and the dough was undercooked.
Our main disappointment stems from the fact that the two main dishes we wanted were sold out before we were seated. Had we known this we would have eaten somewhere else and avoided waiting 30 minutes and eating over cooked eggs.</Review>

<Rate>4< /Rate>< Text>
Rialto Cafe is a popular Breakfast / Brunch Cafe in Downtown Fullerton. It's capacity is about 40-50, so yes it's small, and yes it's popular, so yes you will have to wait. You can't rush people to finish their food, pay and leave. On the other hand, when you do sit down and are paying for a service, you should be served in a appropriate way. The food should come out in timely manner, and yes you shouldn't wait to get your check cuz that won't help the ladder. That's what I experienced at Rialto today, the food is delicious, got the Smaoked dsalmon scrambler and eggs Benedict, both good. I would have them again, but yes I agree with the negative feedback about the service. It's a bit slow, the food takes a long time to come out and they maybe under staffed.

If you don't mind the wait but do want to enjoy some good food them give them a try.</Text>

< review>
Let me by start off by saying that i am 100% Mexican. This is important because i am use to  having the best authentic stews such as; Pozole, Albondigas, caldo de pollo etc... Rialto Cafe has an array of mouth watering soups of the day. Best i have ever had...outside of my moms cooking! I have been there several times after my first visit a month ago, and i have had plenty of great experiences. See you soon Salmon with eggs!</review>

<review>The old Ports 'o Call Village has been torn down.  Only the Fish Market and Ports 'o Call restaurant ate open and the later is to be demolished shortly.  The port is in a 4 to 5 year process of redeveloping this area.  The new name will be San Pedro Marketplace and we all hope it will have the same funky ambiance with small independent shops and non-chain restaurants.  Everyone certainly hopes Ports 'o Call restaurant will return in a new venue.  In the mean time the is still the large working port with ships, cargo cranes, and recreational boats to view.  Some of the harbor tour boats are still running and Los Angeles Maritime Institute is still operating the two brigantine tallships.< /review><time>1521738844364<//time>< Pictures>
